rule.Resources matching.\nfunc ResourceMatches(rule *PolicyRule, combinedRequestedResource, requestedSubresource string) bool {\n\tfor _, ruleResource := range rule.Resources {\n\t\t// if everything is allowed, we match\n\t\tif ruleResource == ResourceAll {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t\t// if we have an exact match, we match\n\t\tif ruleResource == combinedRequestedResource {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\n\t\t// We can also match a */subresource.\n\t\t// if there isn't a subresource, then continue\n\t\tif len(requestedSubresource) == 0 {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\t// if the rule isn't in the format */subresource, then we don't match, continue\n\t\tif len(ruleResource) == len(requestedSubresource)+2 &&\n\t\t\tstrings.HasPrefix(ruleResource, \"*/\") &&\n\t\t\tstrings.HasSuffix(ruleResource, requestedSubresource) {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// SubjectsStrings returns users, groups, serviceaccounts, unknown for display purposes.\nfunc SubjectsStrings(subjects []Subject) ([]string, []string, []string, []string) {\n\tusers := []string{}\n\tgroups := []string{}\n\tsas := []string{}\n\tothers := []string{}\n\n\tfor _, subject := range subjects {\n\t\tswitch subject.Kind {\n\t\tcase ServiceAccountKind:\n\t\t\tsas = append(sas, fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s\", subject.Namespace, subject.Name))\n\n\t\tcase UserKind:\n\t\t\tusers = append(users, subject.Name)\n\n\t\tcase GroupKind:\n\t\t\tgroups = append(groups, subject.Name)\n\n\t\tdefault:\n\t\t\tothers = append(others, fmt.Sprintf(\"%s/%s/%s\", subject.Kind, subject.Namespace, subject.Name))\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn users, groups, sas, others\n}\n\nfunc (r PolicyRule) String() string {\n\treturn \"PolicyRule\" + r.APIGroups)\n\t}\n\tif len(r.Resources) > 0 {\n\t\tformatStringParts = append(formatStringParts, \"Resources:%q\")\n\t\tformatArgs = append(formatArgs, r.Resources)\n\t}\n\tif len(r.NonResourceURLs) A no-no for API types.\n// We use it to construct rules in code. := range subrules {\n\t\tcovered := false\n\t\tfor _, ownerRule := range ownerRules {\n\t\t\tif ruleCovers(ownerRule, subrule) {\n\t\t\t\tcovered = true\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tif !covered {\n\t\t\tuncoveredRules = append(uncoveredRules, subrule)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn (len(uncoveredRules) == 0), uncoveredRules\n}\n\n// BreadownRule takes a rule and builds an equivalent list of rules that each have at most one verb, one\n// resource, and one resource name\nfunc BreakdownRule(rule rbacv1.PolicyRule) []rbacv1.PolicyRule {\n\tsubrules := []rbacv1.PolicyRule{}\n\tfor _, group := range rule.APIGroups {\n\t\tfor _, resource := range rule.Resources {\n\t\t\tfor _, verb := range rule.Verbs {\n\t\t\t\tif len(rule.ResourceNames) > 0 {\n\t\t\t\t\tfor _, resourceName := range rule.ResourceNames {\n\t\t\t\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}, ResourceNames: []string{resourceName}})\n\t\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{APIGroups: []string{group}, Resources: []string{resource}, Verbs: []string{verb}})\n\t\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Non-resource URLs are unique because they only combine with verbs.\n\tfor _, nonResourceURL := range rule.NonResourceURLs {\n\t\tfor _, verb := range rule.Verbs {\n\t\t\tsubrules = append(subrules, rbacv1.PolicyRule{NonResourceURLs: []string{nonResourceURL}, Verbs: []string{verb}})\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn subrules\n}\n\nfunc has(set []string, ele string) bool {\n\tfor _, s := range set {\n\t\tif s == ele {\n\t\t\treturn true\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\nfunc hasAll(set, contains []string) bool {\n\towning := make(map[string]struct{}, len(set))\n\tfor _, ele := range set {\n\t\towning[ele] = struct{}{}\n\t}\n\tfor _, ele := range contains {\n\t\tif _, ok := owning[ele]; !ok {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc resourceCoversAll(setResources, coversResources []string) bool {\n\t// if we have a star or an exact match on all resources, then we match\n\tif has(setResources, rbacv1.ResourceAll) || hasAll(setResources, coversResources) {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, path := range coversResources {\n\t\t// if we have an exact match, then we match.\n\t\tif has(setResources, path) {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\t\t// if we're not a subresource, then we definitely don't match.  fail.\n\t\tif !strings.Contains(path, \"/\") {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t\ttokens := strings.SplitN(path, \"/\", 2)\n\t\tresourceToCheck := \"*/\" + tokens[1]\n\t\tif !has(setResources, resourceToCheck) {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc nonResourceURLsCoversAll(set, covers []string) bool {\n\tfor _, path := range covers {\n\t\tcovered := false\n\t\tfor _, owner := range set {\n\t\t\tif nonResourceURLCovers(owner, path) {\n\t\t\t\tcovered = true\n\t\t\t\tbreak\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t\tif !covered {\n\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn true\n}\n\nfunc nonResourceURLCovers(ownerPath, subPath string) bool {\n\tif ownerPath == subPath {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\treturn strings.HasSuffix(ownerPath, \"*\") && strings.HasPrefix(subPath, strings.TrimRight(ownerPath, \"*\"))\n}\n\n// ruleCovers determines whether the ownerRule (which may have multiple verbs, resources, and resourceNames) covers\n// the subrule (which may only contain at most one verb, resource, and resourceName)\nfunc ruleCovers(ownerRule, subRule rbacv1.PolicyRule) bool {\n\tverbMatches := has(ownerRule.Verbs, rbacv1.VerbAll) || hasAll(ownerRule.Verbs, subRule.Verbs)\n\tgroupMatches := has(ownerRule.APIGroups, rbacv1.APIGroupAll) || hasAll(ownerRule.APIGroups, subRule.APIGroups)\n\tresourceMatches := resourceCoversAll(ownerRule.Resources, subRule.Resources)\n\tnonResourceURLMatches := nonResourceURLsCoversAll(ownerRule.NonResourceURLs, subRule.NonResourceURLs)\n\n\tresourceNameMatches := false\n\n\tif len(subRule.ResourceNames) == 0 {\n\t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0)\n\t} else {\n\t\tresourceNameMatches = (len(ownerRule.ResourceNames) == 0) || hasAll(ownerRule.ResourceNames, subRule.ResourceNames)\n\t}\n\n\treturn verbMatches && groupMatches && resourceMatches && resourceNameMatches && nonResourceURLMatches\n}\n","numLines":174,"startLine":1,"totalLines":174}}}

validation is enforced through a multi-layered mechanism that prevents users from granting permissions they don't hold. The core implementation is distributed across several key files:\\n\\n## Escalation Check Functions\\nThe primary escalation checking logic is in pkg/registry/rbac/escalation_check.go. This file contains three critical functions:\\n\\n1. **EscalationAllowed**: Checks if the user belongs to the 'system:masters' group, which is a superuser group that allows privileged loopback connections and can always perform escalation.\\n\\n2. **RoleEscalationAuthorized**: Explicitly checks if a user has been authorized to perform the 'escalate' verb on Role or ClusterRole resources. This function constructs an AttributesRecord with the 'escalate' verb and queries the authorizer to determine if the decision is Allow.\\n\\n3. **BindingAuthorized**: Checks if a user has the 'bind' verb permission on the specific role being referenced in a RoleBinding or ClusterRoleBinding.\\n\\n## Policy-Based Storage Enforcement\\nEscalation validation is enforced at the storage layer in four policybased storage implementations:\\n\\n1. **pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrole/policybased/storage.go**: Prevents creation/update of ClusterRoles with escalating permissions. For ClusterRoles with aggregationRules, it requires cluster-admin privileges (full authority on *).\\n\\n2. **pkg/registry/rbac/clusterrolebinding/policybased/storage.go**: Validates ClusterRoleBinding creation/update by checking if the user either has escalation allowed, explicit bind authorization, or owns the permissions in the referenced ClusterRole.\\n\\n3. **pkg/registry/rbac/role/policybased/storage.go**: Validates Role creation/update with the same escalation checks as ClusterRoles (namespaced variant).\\n\\n4. **pkg/registry/rbac/rolebinding/policybased/storage.go**: Validates RoleBinding creation/update (namespaced variant).\\n\\n## Permission Coverage Validation\\nThe core escalation prevention logic is in pkg/registry/rbac/validation/rule.go through the **ConfirmNoEscalation** function. This function:\\n\\n1. Extracts the user from context\\n2. Calls the RuleResolver to get all rules the user currently has\\n3. Returns an error if the user is attempting to grant permissions not currently held\\n\\nThe **Covers** function performs the actual permission comparison by:\\n1. Breaking down servant rules into atomic rule tuples (one verb, resource, and resource name per rule)\\n2. Checking if each atomic rule is covered by at least one owner rule\\n3. Verifying that wildcards and exact matches are properly evaluated for verbs, API groups, resources, and resource names\\n\\n## Version Adaptation\\nThe pkg/registry/rbac/validation/internal_version_adapter.go file provides **ConfirmNoEscalationInternal** which converts internal version PolicyRules to v1 PolicyRules before calling ConfirmNoEscalation, enabling consistent validation across API versions.\\n\\n## Rule Compaction\\nThe pkg/registry/rbac/validation/policy_compact.go file provides **CompactRules** which optimizes error messages by consolidating simple rules that only differ by verbs, reducing the verbosity of escalation denial error messages.\\n\\n## Bootstrap Policies\\nThe plugin/pkg/auth/authorizer/rbac/bootstrappolicy/controller_policy.go file defines default bootstrap ClusterRoles that include the 'escalate' verb for specific system controllers (like the clusterrole-aggregation-controller) that need permission to mutate ClusterRoles in specific ways.\\n\\n## Attack Prevention\\nThis implementation prevents privilege escalation by:\\n1.
